THAILAND
ELECTRICITY GENERATING AUTHORITY OF THAILAND
APPRAISAL OF THE
BAN CHAO NEN HYDRO-ELECTRIC PROJECT
(QUAE YAI HYDRO-ELECTRIC PROJECT)
SUMMARY AND CONCLUSIONS
i.        This report appraises the first phase of the Ban Chao Nen Hydro-
electric Project in Thailand, needed to meet a growing demand for power
and energy. Initial installed capacity will be 360 MW in three units with
an annual capability of 1,230 GWh. Provision will be made for the in-
stallation of two additional 180 MW reversible pump-turbine units in the
mid-1980's. The project also includes the erection of about 165 km of
230 kV transmission lines to link the scheme to the load center.
ii.       The project, essentially multipurpose, is a logical consequence
of a Bank Loan made in 1964 to finance the first stage (175,000 ha) of a
comprehensive Meklong Basin Irrigation Development Program downstream of
Ban Chao Nen. It will permit dry season irrigation of this first stage
but will also guarantee wet and provide for dry season irrigation of an
additional 230,000 ha.
iii.      The total cost of the project to be constructed in the period
1974-1979 is estimated at about US$181.0 million including interest during
construction. Parallel financing with the Japanese Overseas Economic
Cooperation Fund (OECF) is envisaged. OECF has agreed to finance the
foreign exchange and some local costs of the hydraulic and electro-mechanical
equipment, transmission lines and engineering consulting services, estimated
at about US$41.0 million. Accordingly, the Government has requested a Bank
loan of US$75.0 million equivalent to finance the foreign costs of civil
works and interest during construction on the Bank-financed portion. The
inclusion of interest during construction is justified because of the
financial requirements of the Borrower. The balance of about US$65.0 million
equivalent or about 36% of the total costs would be financed by the Govern-
ment and the Borrower.
iv.       The Borrower would be the Electricity Generating Authority of
Thailand (EGAT), established in 1968 by the merger of three existing
generating authorities. The proposed loan would represent the seventh loan
for projects involving power. Experience with previous loans has been
satisfactory.
v.        Economic growth was substantial in the 1960's, the increase in
real GDP averaging 8% per year. Growth slowed to 6% in 1970-71 and was
further reduced in 1972 by a drought that severely restricted agricultural



- ii -
production. For 1972-1976 the Government's target for GDP growth is 7%
annually and resumption of real growth at a rate of 6-8% is expected in
1974. Agriculture is the major economic activity (1/3 of GDP, employing
80% of the labor force, providing 70% of export earnings). Manufacturing
is small (1/8 of GDP, employing 4% of the labor force) but is growing
rapidly at 10% per annum.
vi.       The responsibility for the sector rests with three authorities:
EGAT, responsible for major generation; the Metropolitan Electricity
Authority (MEA), responsible for the distribution of electricity in the
Bangkok Metropolitan Area; and the Provincial Electricity Authority (PEA),
responsible for generation in remote areas and distribution in the rest
of the country. The sector as a whole is well-operated, investments are
adequate and reasonable, and future prospects are good,
vii.      By the end of 1972 EGAT had installed about 1,400 MW of generating
capacity and accounted for over 95% of all electrical energy generated in
Thailand and by 1982 will account for nearly 98%. Of the energy available to
EGAT for sale in 1972, direct sales to a number of industrial consumers
accounted for 7%; sales to MEA for about 70%; and to PEA for about 23%.
In 1982 direct sales are forecast to account for about 3.5%; sales to MEA
for 71%; and sales to PEA for 25.5%. From 1968-1972 EGAT's generation
requirements increased at an average annual growth rate of 21.0%.  For
1972-1982 a growth rate of 13.0% is forecast reflecting the substantially
larger base. Thus in 1982 maximum demand to be served by EGAT is forecast
at 3,260 MW and generation requirements at 19,250 GWH. In 1982 EGAT will
have in service about 4,000 MW of which about 3,800 MW will be dependable.
The project, therefore, represents about 13.8% of the capacity to be
installed between 1973-1982.
viii.     EGAT's planned 1973-85 expansion program includes investments
totalling about US$1,450 million for the 1974-82 period. The proposed
project would account for 13.0% of this total. Both MEA and PEA have
developed five-year expansion programs, their investments are considered
adequate and the relationship between generation and transmission, and
distribution is reasonable.
ix.       As previously mentioned, the project is essentially multipurpose.
Although it is justified on power alone, assurances have been obtained
from the Government in connection with the Chao Phya Irrigation Improve-
ment Project (Credit 379-TH), that consultants would be engaged to assist
in finalizing a feasibility study and in preparing a report on a Meklong
Irrigation Improvement Project with the objective of maximizing the
benefits to the economy made possible by the project. The economic rate
of return for the project, with all costs allocated to power, has a mean
value of at least 12.9% and with a reasonable allocation of common costs
to irrigation/agriculture, of at least 18.3%. As a multipurpose project the
rate of return varies on a sensitivity basis from not less than 12.3% to
21.7%. The computed rates are satisfactory. They are based on fuel prices
prevailing in July 1973. A recalculation utilizing current fuel prices
indicates that the 12.9% rate of return given above would increae to at
least 18%.



- iii -
x.        EGAT's tanagement is able, and its staff is competent.  Its
present financial situation is good. The rate of return has been about
9%; debt service coverage was better than 1.6; self-financing has equalled
30%; and the 58/42 debt/equity ratio indicates a satisfactory capital
structure. Its future financial situation, because of the substantial
investment program and rising fuel costs is not as favorable. Because of
the uncertainty as to fuel price development, a fuel adjustment clause
has been agreed to automatically pass on to the consumers any fuel price
increases subsequent to an increase in basic tariffs in 1974 to cover the
increased price of fuel oil since July 1973. Together with continued
exemption from income tax EGAT's forecast financial situation is satisfactory.
EGAT will provide for about 30% of all investments needed in 1974-82, the
rate of return will exceed 10% for 5 out of the 9 forecast years, will not
fall below 8%, and the debt/equity ratio will not exceed 59/41.
xi.       The proposed project would be a suitable basis for a Bank Loan
of US$75.0 million equivalent for a period of 26 years, including a period
of grace of 6 years corresponding to the construction period.






THAILAND
ELECTRICITY GENERATING AUTHORITY OF THAILAND
APPRAISAL OF THE
BAN CHAO NEN HYDRO-ELECTRIC PROJECT
(QUAE YAI HYDRO-ELECTRIC PROJECT)
I. INTRODUCTION
1.01      The Government of Thailand on behalf of the Electricity Generating
Authority of Thailand (EGAT) has requested a Bank Loan of US$75.0 million
equivalent to help finance the Quae Yai Hydro-Electric project estimated
to cost about US$181.0 million equivalent including interest during con-
struction. About US$116.0 million would represent foreign exchange costs
and about US$65.0 million local currency costs. The Government has also
requested financial assistance from the Japanese Overseas Economic
Development Fund (OECF). OECF has agreed to provide a loan of about
Yen 11,600 million (equivalent to about US$41.0 million) on an untied
basis to finance the foreign exchange costs of all the electro-mechanical
and hydraulic equipment, transmission line, and engineering consulting
services required for the project, estimated to total about US$37.0 million,
plus local cost financing equivalent to about US$4.0 million. The balance
of about US$65.0 million equivalent would be financed through internal
cash generation, a Government contribution and local borrowings. Thus Bank
participation would be limited to the financing of the foreign exchange costs
of construction equipment and civil works (US$57.0 million); and interest
during construction on the Bank financed portion (US$18.0 million).
1.02      The potential for irrigation development and power generation in
the Meklong River Basin was recognized as early as 1903. The first major
development program was initiated with Bank Loan 394-TH of US$22.0 million
in 1964. This consisted of the first stage of a comprehensive Meklong
Basin Irrigation Development prepared by the Royal Irrigation Department
(RID). This project provided for the construction of the Vajiralongkorn
diversion barrage and navigation locks; canal headworks; flood protection
dikes; a main feeder canal and concrete lined main canals and lateral
systems to serve about 175,000 ha; 40 km of feeder roads; and drainage
canals. Benefits were based on wet season irrigation and flood control.
The proposed project is a logical consequence of this first loan, guaran-
teeing wet and providing for dry season irrigation of a further 230,000 ha
and enabling dry season benefits to be achieved on the original 175,000 ha.
Land use would average about 160%. (Further details on the possible irri-
gation project are given in Annex 1.)
1.03      In connection with the Chao Phya Irrigation Improvement Project
of 1973 (Credit 379-TH), agreement was reached with the Thai Authorities
that consultants would be engaged by the Ministry of Agriculture to provide



-2-
technical assistance to finalize a feasibility study and to prepare a
report on a MekIong Irrigation Improvement Project for submission to the
Bank. This report has the objective of defining an irrigation project
in order to maximize the benefits to the economy provided by the proposed
project. The proposed project is, however, justified on power alone and
accordingly it is proposed that the loan be made to EGAT.
1.04      In 1966 the Yanhee Electricity Authority (YEA), EGAT's predecessor,
requested technical assistance under the Colombo Plan for investigations of
the hydro-electric potential of the Quae Yai River Basin. In 1967 a contract
was signed between YEA and the Electric Power Development Co., Ltd., of
Tokyo (EPDC) to prepare a feasibility report.
1.05      A feasibility report became available to the Bank in 1970 and
was discussed with EGAT and EPDC. The report was not convincing as
to the physical feasibility of the project and further investigations
were considered essential. These have been made and to assist and guide
such investigations EGAT appointed an international board of consultants
(ICB). At its last meeting in April 1972, the consultants concluded that
these supplementary investigations established the project's technical
viability beyond reasonable doubt. Design changes made in the interim
period further improved the project. (Further details on the ICB's
activities are given in Annex 2.)
1.06      The proposed loan would be the Bank's twenty-fifth to Thailand
and its seventh for projects involving electric power. The most recent
power loan (790-TH) was made in November 1971 to help finance thermal unit
No. 4 at South Bangkok. Prior to this a loan was made in early 1970
(655-TH) to help finance the Sirikit hydro-electric power project and thermal
unit No. 3 at South Bangkok. Construction of all three projects is pro-
ceeding satisfactorily.
1.07      This report is based on a feasibility report prepared for EGAT
by its consultants, on information provided by EGAT, and Qn the findings
of a Bank mission composed of Messrs. E. A. Minnig (Power Engineer),
A. N. Memon (Financial Analyst) and Messrs. T. Samuels, M. Ben David, and
P. Judd (Agriculture/Irrigation Consultants), which visited Thailand in
November/December 1972 and a reappraisal made by Messrs. Minnig and J. M.
Sneddon (Financial Analyst) in July 1973.
II. THE COUNTRY, TEiE ECONOMY AND THE SECTOR
THE COUNTRY AND THE ECONOMY
2.01      The Kingdom of Thailand is 514,000 km2 in area and had a population
of 38 million in 1972, which is growing at a rate of 3% per year. Per capita
GNP was about US$210 in 1972 and electricity generation amounted to 153 kwh
per capita. Economic growth was substantial in the 1960's, the increase
in real CDP averaging 8% per year. Growth slowed to 6% in 1970-71, largely



- 3 -
as a result of weak export demand, and was further reduced in 1972 by a
drought that severely restricted agricultural production. The Government's
Third Five-Year Plan (1972-76) establishes a target of 7% annual growth in
GDP, and resumption of real growth at a rate of 7-8% is expected in 1974.
Bangkok and the central region have developed more rapidly than the other
areas of the country, and one objective of the Third Five-Year Plan is to
promote the development of the less advanced regions.
2.02      Thailand is well endowed with land and water resources for agri-
cultural production. Agriculture is the major economic activity, contributing
about one-third of GDP, employing 80% of the labor force, and providing about
70% of merchandise export earnings. The manufacturing sector is small (13%
of GDP and 4% of employment) but growing fairly rapidly at about 10% per
year. Significant tourism development is also taking place, and tourism is
now a major source of foreign exchange earnings.
THE SECTOR
General
2.03      The development of the sector is carried out by three independent
authorities. The Electricity Generating Authority of Thailand (EGAT); the
Metropolitan Electricity Authority (MEA); and the Provincial Electricity
Authority (PEA).
2.04      The power sector is well operated, investments are adequate and
reasonable, and future prospects are good. In 1972 electricity generation
totalled 5,990 GWh and maximum demand 1,117 MW. However, only about 17%
of the total population or 6.4 million, of which 3.6 million were within the
Metropolitan Area of Bangkok, directly enjoyed the benefits of electricity.
By 1982, Thailand's electrical energy requirements are forecast to total
about 19,700 GWh with a maximum demand of about 3,400 MW. It is estimated
that about 27% of the population would benefit from electricity in this
year and an increasing percentage of the total would be outside Bangkok.
Compared with average annual growth rates achieved from 1968-1972 of
20.5% for generation and 18.2% for maximum demand, the forecast growth
rates 1972-1982 are 12.6% and 12.0% respectively reflecting primarily a
larger base but also a lower economic growth rate. However, a substantial
rural electrification program would be undertaken during the period (see
para 2.14).
Energy Requirement and Resources
2.05      During the period 1956-1970 total energy consumption in Thailand
increased at an average annual growth rate of 13% p.a. to reach about 6.3
million tons petroleum equivalent in 1970. It is forecast that the past
growth rate will be sustained until at least 1990 and that by 1980 total
energy consumption will amount to 27.1 million tons petroleum equivalent
with petroleum products accounting for about 80%.



-4-
2.06      Thailand's energy resources consist of hydro-power, limited
petroleum and coal, large but as yet not economically exploitable oil
shale deposits, charcoal, wood, paddy husk, and bagasse. Its hydro-
potential totals about 11,300 MW and 40,700 GWh (excluding the potential
on two international rivers, the Mekong and the Salaween) of which only
about 520 MW or 4.6% is presently exploited. Coal deposits are
estimated at about 150 million tons of which about 65 million tons can
be commercially exploited. Proven reserves of petroleum total about
2.5 million barrels (estimated consumption of petroleum products in 1975
are 78.3 million barrels) but exploration is being carried out in the
Northeast and in the Gulf of Siam. Oil shale deposits are estimated at
about 2,700 million barrels which, if economically exploitable, could meet
Thailand's domestic requirements at the current rate of consumption for up
to 50 years. In 1970 coal, charcoal, wood, paddy husk and bagasse accounted
for only 10% of total energy requirements; the main energy sources were
petroleum (80%) and hydro power (10%) (further details are given in Annex 3).
2.07      A future potential source of power for EGAT could be from hydro
facilities constructed on the Mekong River. The hydro-electric potential
of this river and its tributaries is substantial. The first phase of the
135 MW Namn Ngum project on a tributary in Laos was completed in early 1972
and EGAT has been receiving energy from it since. The Pa Mong project on
the Mekong River about 18 miles from Vientiane, where it forms the border
between Thailand and Laos, has a potential of 2,800-4,800 MW. However, the
earliest date by which Pa Mong power might be available is in the late 1980's.
The Electricity Generating Authority of Thailand (EGAT)
2.08      EGAT was established in 1968 by the merger of three former
public electricity authorities: the Yanhee Electricity Authority (YEA);
the Northeast Electricity Authority (NEEA); and the Lignite Authority (LA).
YEA was established in 1957 as a condition of the first power loan to
Thailand. The purpose of the Act establishing EGAT was to increase the
efficiency of electricity supply throughout the country and to coordinate
the generation and transmission systems.
2.09      EGAT is now responsible for most generation and transmission in
the public sector. It accounted for 95.3% of all electrical energy
generated in Thailand in 1972, the balance being generated by PEA in
power systems isolated from the national grid (1.8%), and by private
generating plants (2.9%). EGAT sells energy in bulk to MEA, PEA, and
to large industrial consumers.
The Metropolitan Electricity Authority (MEA)
2.10      MEA, a state enterprise, was established in 1958 with the
objective of supplying electricity to the provinces of Bangkok, Thonburi
Nonthaburi and Samut Prakon. In 1972 MEA was serving nearly 400,000 con-
sumers with a maximum demand of about 640 MW and sales of about 3,500 GWh
(67% of the national total). Of the energy sold, about 18% was used for
residential domestic purposes, about 81% by industrial and comercial



enterprises, and about 1% for street lighting. MEA, EGAT's largest
consumer, purchases all energy requirements from it and in 1972 accounted
for about 70% of EGAT's sales.
2.11      MEA's distribution investment program 1972-1976 totals about
1,800 million Baht or about US$90.0 million equivalent. It is designed
to meet the increasing demand for power and energy in the area presently
supplied and also to expand the system within the franchise area to areas
presently without service. Planned investment per kW of incremental
demand of about US$150 is considered reasonable and adequate.
2.12      MEA's financial situation is satisfactory with earnings forecast
to provide a rate of return on average net fixed assets in operation of
about 11% yearly for 1972-1976. Its average revenue in 1972 of about 1.97
US cents/kwh is forecast to drop to 1.8 US cents/kwh by 1976 primarily due
to two planned reductions of about 2% in 1973 and 1975 made possible by
economies of scale and improved load factor. The probable effect of the
recent oil price increases on MEA's tariffs is given in paragraph 3.11
(further details on MEA's operations are given in Annex 4).
The Provincial Electricity Authority (PEA)
2.13      PEA, a state enterprise established in 1960, is authorized to
distribute electricity for residential, commercial and industrial use in
the whole of Thailand (service area of MEA excepted). PEA purchases
energy in bulk from EGAT and also generates electricity in areas that
cannot be economically connected to the EGAT system. In 1972, PEA
served about 570,000 consumers with a maximum demand of about 340 MW and
sales of about 1,200 GWh. Of its energy requirements, 88% were purchased
from EGAT representing 23% of EGAT's sales and 12% were locally generated.
Of the energy sold, 34% was used for residential domestic purposes, 65%
for industrial and commercial use, and about 1% for street lighting.
2.14      PEA's investment program 1972-1976 totals about 1,370 million
Baht or US$66.0 million equivalent. These investments, covering an
incremental demand of about 310 MW, are equivalent to about US$213/kW,
substantially higher than MEA's, but not unreasonably so given its vast
service area and the relatively high investments foreseen for rural
electrification (2,500 villages with 44 consumers each on average, total
initial costs about US$22.5 million or US$9,000/village).
2.15      PEA's financial position is reasonable given the nature of its
activities. Its tariffs, reflecting the higher cost of service, are
substantially higher than MEA's producing average revenues equivalent to
about US cents 3.24/kwh in 1972 or about 1.6 times higher than MEA's.
Nevertheless, since its establisthment in 1960, PEA has been able to lower
tariffs almost yearly because of economies of scale, substitution of low
cost energy from EGAT for diesel generation and an improving load factor.
The probable effect of the recent oil price increases on PEA's tariffs is
given in paragraph 3.11 (further details on PEA's operations are given
in Annex 5).



-6-
III. THE BORROWER
3.01      EGAT would be the Borrower and the Government of Thailand the
Guarantor.
Organization and Management
3.02      The 1968 Act establishing EGAT provides for a Board of Directors
consisting of a Chairman and not more than ten other members, including
ex-officio, the General Manager. The Chairman and other members of the
Board are appointed by the Council of Ministers for four year terms. The
General Manager, who is appointed by the Board subject to the approval of
the Council of Ministers, administers EGAT in accordance with policies
determined by the Board.
3.03      One important provision of the Act deals with the operation of
hydro plants associated with multipurpose projects. Section 30 of the Act
gives EGAT the responsibility for the operation of multipurpose dams and
requires EGAT and the Royal Irrigation Department (RID) to jointly issue
regulations concerning the storage volume to be retained and the volume
of water to be released from such storages. This is to reconcile the
sometimes conflicting water release patterns required for power and
irrigation and to optimize the joint use.
3.04      The existing Loan Agreements stipulate that repeal or material
amendment of the 1968 Act without the prior agreement of the Bank, would
contribute an event of default. A similar provision is included in the
Agreement for the proposed Loan.
3.05      At the end of 1972, EGAT had a total work force of 10,427 of
which 6,464 were permanent and 3,963 were temporary, mostly engaged on
construction. Of the permanent staff, about 900, or 14% are university
graduates and about 1,000, or 15%, are graduates of higher vocational
schools. A training program exists to develop the various skills required
(see Annex 6). EGAT's operational staff is well trained and competent.
Although the number of employees is slightly higher (7% - 10%) than
considered necessary, this is due to the transfer to EGAT of the staff of
its predecessors, a situation which, however, improves yearly due to
attrition and system expansion.
3.06      The General Manager is well qualified and exceptionally dynamic.
The organization functions smoothly, the working climate and personnel
relations are excellent, and as a result dedication to work is high.
EGAT's organization is shown in Annex 7.
3.07      The work load of the Financial Controller is heavy and there is
a need, as recommended by EGAT's financial consultants, Messrs. Cooper
and Lybrand, in their 1971 annual report, to strengthen the Accounting
and Finance Department by the recruitment of a second Assistant Controller.



-7-
The General Manager recognizes this, but efforts to recruit a suitable
person have failed in the past. Nevertheless, EGAT has agreed to renew
its recruitment efforts.
Accounting and Audit
3.08      The provisions of the Act and the way they have been administered
have been effective in maintaining the sound financial position which has
characterized EGAT's operations. EGAT follows the "Uniform System of
Accounts" established by the US Federal Power Commission. The accounts are
administered effectively and annual statements are prepared within the
period stipulated by the Act (90 days after the close of the Fiscal Year).
The Act also requires the appointment of auditors. Since 1966 an indepen-
dent accounting firm, Messrs. Cooper and Lybrand (UK) has been retained
by EGAT and its predecessors to assist the Government Audit Council, which
prepares the formal audit. This arrangement has been satisfactory and in
agreement with the provisions of previous Bank Loans. The relevant covenant
has been repeated in the proposed loan.
Tariffs
3.09      The 1968 Act requires that tariffs should cover (i) all operating
expenses including employees' benefits and bonuses, depreciation and
interest; (ii) amortization in excess of depreciation and increases in
the cost of asset replacement; and (iii) reasonable allocations to a
contingency reserve, and financing of a substantial portion of system
expansion investments. Loan Agreement 790-TH requires EGAT to self-
finance on average, 30% of its capital investment program. This has been
satisfactory in the past and a similar covenant has been repeated in the
Agreement for the proposed loan.
3.10      EGAT's tariffs, of the standard demand-energy type which charges
consumers separately for their demand (KW) and energy (kwh), are appropriate
for a supplier of bulk power. The average level of tariffs in 1972 was
29 stang/kwh (US cents 1.4/kwh) which was reasonable in view of the rela-
tively high cost of fuel even then (US cents 50/million BTU, including taxes).
3.11      Periodic reductions in the tariffs of EGAT, MEA, and PEA were
made during the last decade because of improved efficiency and increased
sales. They did not adversely affect the financial viability of the
organizations. However, in view of rising construction costs, the substan-
tial expansion program and recent currency exchange rate. changes, a tariff
increase of about 5% will be required to satisfy the 30% self-financing
target. This will be additional to a fuel adjustment surcharge designed
to recover all variations in fuel costs above the 1973 base. Present
estimates indicate that the surcharge will increase the cost per kwh sold
by EGAT during the second half of 1974 by about 55%, as compared to 1973.
As a result HEA's cost per kwh sold will increase about 40Z and PEA's about
25%, but these increases are not expected to apply uniformly to all consumers.
Small residential consumers may hardly be affected but rates to comercial



-8-
consumers (offices, hotels, entertainment, etc.) are likely to iAcrease
substantially. However, the bulk of the additional revenue required is
expected to come from industrial consumers. As the cost of electric
energy for most of these represents only a very small part of the cost
of production, even a doubling of industrial rates would have a relatively
small effect on the cost of the finished product.
Insurance
3.12      An existing covenant requiring EGAT to maintain reasonable
insurance coverage has been followed. This covenant is repeated in the
Agreement for the proposed loan.
Existing Facilities
3.13      At the end of calendar 1972 EGAT had a total of 1,424 NW in
service. Of this total 515 MW were hydro; 704 MW steam thermal; 165 MW
gas turbines; and 40 MW diesel. Transmission is carried out at three
voltage levels; 230 kV, 115 kV, and 69 kV, with a total length of 4,549 km.
69 substations were in service with an installed transformer capacity of
2,345 MVA. Of these, 8 serve MEA; 55 serve PEA; and 6 serve large
industrial consumers. Given the rapid expansion of EGAT's system, facil-
ities are new, modern, and efficient. Plant is well opeoated and mainte-
nance satisfactory.
3.14      At the end of 1972 EGAT had five generating plants under
construction with a total installed capacity of 1,024 MW (394 MW hydro
and 630 MW thermal). Annex 8 gives further details and the map attached
to the report shows the location of generating plant and the trapuwission
system.
Development Strategy
3.15      EGAT has prepared a program covering the years 1973-1965 to meet
its forecast market requirements. This program is reasonable, is based on
least cost solutions and provides adequate flexibility. The preent system
is subdivided into four regions identified on the attached map. Whilst
Regions 1, 2 and 4 are interconnected, Region 3 still operates in isolation.
In Region 1 and 4 base load is provided by oil thermal plants located to the
North and South of Bangkok, the major load center. Base load cap also be
provided by the Mae Moh lignite fired plant in the North. Hydro generation
(Bhumipol) covers intermediate load requirements, whilst gas-turbines and
diesel units located at load centers are used for peaking, thus reducing
transmission losses. Region 2 is mainly served by hydro generation and
surplus energy is imported through this Region from the Nam Ng"u Iydro-project
in Laos. In Region 3, all generation is presently thermal (lignite fired,
diesel, and gas turbines). To ease the situation brought about by the recent
substantial increases in the price of fuel oil, EGAT proposes to convert an
existing 75 MW oil-fired unit at North Bangkok to utilize local lignite apd
to advance the commissioning of the proposed New Mae Moh 75 MW lpigito fired
steam unit No. 2 by two years.



- 9 -
3.16      EGAT's system is expected to be interconnected by 1979 with
the completion of the Region 1 - 3 tie line. This will increase operational
flexibility and permit maximum economy in system operation.
3.17      The major hydro plants are operated from multipurpose reservoirs
with irrigation demand given priority. The mixed hydro-thermal system
has enabled EGAT to fully utilize hydro capability. Thus in the dry season
when irrigation demand is highest, hydro plants operate at a high plant
factor and the output of thermal plants is reduced. In the wet season
when irrigation demand is low and storage drawn down, the release of water
is minimal and hydro plants operate at a. low plant factor. Hydro power
capability can virtually be maintained throughout the year.
3.18      EGAT calculates its firm  capacity as dependable hydro capability
plus thermal installed capacity less the largest unit out of service for
maintenance. This is acceptable. The following illustrates the reserve
position:

3.19      EGAT's capital investment program through 1982 totals about
9 29,200 million (US$1,450 million). Incremental costs/kW amount to about
US$419, which is reasonable since investments include transmission and
substations in addition to generation. The proposed project accounts for
about 13% of investments up to 1982. Annex 9 shows EGAT's forecast demand
and the commissioning of new facilities in diagramatic form; Annex 10 gives
details of plant commissioning in tabular form; and Annex 11 gives the annual
construction expenditures for each project.



- 10 -
IV. THE PROJECT
The Project
4.01      The project, located about 80 km upstream of Kanchanaburi and
150 km Northwest of Bangkok, will consist of a 140 m high and 615 m long
rock-fill dam with a total embankment volume of about 13 million m3. The
reservoir, extending about 120 km upstream, will store about 17,000 million
m3.  Effective storage of about 4,400 million m3 will equal about 1 year's
average inflow. An open channel chute-type spillway controlled by five
radial gates will be located on the right abutment. The intake structure,
adjacent to the spillway, will have five intakes; three will be operational
in the first phase. Three 120 m3/sec capacity penstocks will lead to a
surface powerhouse located below the dam. In the first phase the power-
house will accommodate three 120 MW/140 NVA units.  A second phase (mid
1980's) will add two 180 MW reversible pump-turbine units. Transformers
will be located outdoors on the tailrace side of the powerhouse and a
switchyard will be provided on the left bank. The 360 MW station output
will be tied to the system grid over two 165 km long, 230 kV circuits.
Communication equipment, construction equipment necessary to carry out
preliminary works and resettlement, and engineering consulting services
complete the project which is scheduled for covmissioning in 1980. (Annex
12 provides further details.)
4.02      On attaining equilibrium operating conditions, the energy
capability of the project averages 1,230 GWh annually, giving an average
annual plant factor of 39%. The maximum monthly plant factor will be
about 90% (dry season, when irrigation requirements are high) and the
minimum monthly plant factor about 15% (wet season, when irrigation
requirements are low).
Financing Arrangements
4.03      The Japanese Overseas Economic Cooperation Fund (OECF) has
agreed to finance, on an untied basis, the foreign exchange cost of all
hydraulic equipment (gates, valves, penstock, etc.,); electro-mechanical
equipment (turbines, generators, transformers, cranes, etc.,); transmission
line and substations; engineering consulting services; and associated
contingencies. In addition, OECF has agreed to finance some local costs.
The proposed Bank loan would finance the foreign exchange cost of: (i)
construction equipment required by EGAT to carry out preliminary works and
resettlement; (ii) the main civil works; (iii) associated contingencies;
and (iv) interest during construction on the Bank financed portion. The
remaining balance covering local costs and interest during construction on
the OECF financed portion would be financed by the Government of Thailand
and EGAT. OECF agreed on February 20, 1974 to provide EGAT with a letter
of intent specifying the items to be financed prior to the conclusion of
a formal agreement(s). This is an acceptable arrangement and a condition
of effectiveness of the proposed loan would be the issuance of such a
letter of intent by OECF.

on exchange rates prevailing as of mid-February 1974:

- 12 -
The extensive physical investigations carried out during the past four years
(paragraph 4.10) have allowed project design to evolve to an advanced stage.
The cost estimate shown above results from a good understanding of site
conditions, a well honed design and benefits from the fact that bids for
the major civil works contract have already been received. The cost esti-
mate is significantly higher (about 90%) than an earlier estimate prepared
in 1968 and takes into account exchange rates prevailing at mid-February
1974. For items to be financed by the proposed Bank loan physical contin-
gencies represent about 12% of basic costs, subdivided as follows: (i) a
50% contingency for foundation treatment; (ii) a 5% overall contingency for
increased quantities; and (iii) a 3% overall contingency for environmental
considerations - rehabilitation of borrow areas (concrete aggregates and
earthfill) and quarries. The price increase contingency for items to be
financed by the proposed Bank loan is limited to about 5% of basic costs
since bid prices are fixed with unit rates not subject to adjustment.
Physical contingencies of about 5% and price contingencies of about 33%
of basic costs are included for items to be financed by OECF. The resulting
total contingency -- physical and price -- represents about 21% of basic
February 1974 costs and is considered adequate provided that exchange rates
do not fluctuate significantly from their mid-February 1974 level. A de-
tailed cost estimate is given in Annex 13.
Procurement and Disbursement
4.05      All materials, equipment and contractors' services will be pro-
cured on the basis of international competitive bidding with the exception
of contractors' services for preliminary works and resettlement. These
will be carried out by EGAT work force, supplemented by local contractors.
The Bank's Procurement Guidelines will be followed for items financed by
the proposed loan. Procurement Guidelines established by OECF will be
utilized for items financed by it. OECF's guidelines are similar to the
Bank's in all major respects. Disbursements from the proposed loan would
be made against c.i.f. cost of directly imported equipment and materials,
or 100% of total expenditures ex-factory for equipment and materials
manufactured locally, and 65% of total expenditures for imported equipment
and materials procured locally. Disbursements on the Main Civil Works
Contract would be at 60% of total expenditures representing the foreign
exchange component. Should there be any savings these would be cancelled.
A disbursement schedule is given in Annex 14.
Consulting Services
4.06      EGAT has contracted with EPDC to continue as its prime consultants
and proposes to retain the services of individual members of the Interna-
tional Consulting Board. These arrangements and the terms of contract are
satisfactory. Nevertheless, agreement was obtained during negotiations
that EGAT will continue to employ consultants acceptable to the Bank
throughout the construction period of the project.



- 13 -
Construction Schedule
4.07      Specifications and tender documents for the Civil Works contract
were issued with Bank approval in September 1973, bids were received on
December 19, 1973, and the contract will be awarded mid-April 1974. The
bid evaluation was reviewed and agreed by the Bank. For equipment contracts,
tenders would be issued in mid-1974 and contracts awarded in early 1975. It
is estimated that filling of the reservoir could commence with the 1977 wet
season. This is a critical date since missing this season would delay
commissioning by one year. Resettlement activities would be concentrated
over the years 1975-1978. The units are scheduled to be commissioned in
August and November 1979 and March 1980. Thus total construction time is
about 6 years and is considered reasonable. A detailed construction
program is shown in Annex 15.
Hydrology
4.08      Hydrology is based on a twenty-year period of record (1952-1971)
of 5 stream flow gauging stations. Available data were verified by com-
paring the simultaneous run-off at the various gauging stations. A good
correlation was established between average run-off and average rainfall.
Maximum probable flood calculations made using well recognized methods,
indicate a peak flood of about 7,100 m3/sec and a volume of about 3,800
million m3. (Further details are provided in Annex 16.)
4.09      The rate of reservoir filling is critical, because irrigation needs
have to be met prior to commencement of generation. An analysis made to
determine the probability of filling showed that the reservoir will first
reach its mean operating level with a 95% probability by March 1985, or
with a 50% probability in March 1982. This confirmed that the progress
rate assumed for agriculture development downstream and thus water release
patterns for irrigation were reasonable. (Further details are provided in
Annex 17.)
Geology
4.10      The design of the project is based on substantial investigations.
27 exploratory adits with a total length of 1,240 m were excavated and
45 drill holes with a total length of 2,740 m made. EGAT also carried out a
grout testing program from January - July 1973 to provide prospective bidders
with additional information to assist them in preparing realistic tenders.
4.11      Particular attention was given to a potential reservoir leakage
problem because of geological conditions. Extensive investigations showed,
however, that this was not a serious risk. Dam foundation conditions are
more critical. There is a large weak zone in the middle part of the left
abutment. Besides a grout curtain (up to 70 m deep) to prevent leakage,
blanket grouting will be carried out to improve the mechanical properties
of the foundation surface layer and a core cut-off trench will be provided.
In addition a foundation gallery will be provided for the lower parts of
the right and left abutments and under the river bed to serve maintenance
and inspection purposes. (Further details are given in Annex 18.)



- 14 -
Ecology
4.12      EGAT engaged the Asian Institute of Technology (AIT) (Bangkok) in
1972 to carry out an Ecological Reconnaissance. A 35-man team covering the
following disciplines -- Fisheries, Acquatic Plants, Archaelogy, Forestry,
Social Science, Tropical Medicine, and Water and Agricultural Engineering
produced a preliminary report in November 1972. This exceptionally well-
prepared report dealt with Water Resource Management; Mining; Forestry;
River Basin Development; Resettlement; Health; Fisheries; Acquatic Weeds;
Archaelogical sites; Tourism; and Environmental Aspects. The report concludes
that "it is considered that there is no single ecological consequence, ot
combination of consequences, which is of sufficient importance to preclude
construction of the Project." The report, however, made certain recorenda-
tions and suggestions for further investigations which EGAT followed. A
subsequent report prepared by AIT entitled "Selected Ecological Surveys"
dated January 1974 covered: Dry Season Water-borne Parasitic Diseases;
Heavy Metal Pollution; Aesthetic Qualities of the Quai Yai Basin; and
Archaeology. During negotiations agreement was reached that all reasonable
measures would be taken to ensure that execution and operation of the
Project are carried out with due regard to ecological and environmental
factors and, in particular, the recommendations of the AIT reports.
4.13      A total number of 8,000 inhabitants will need to be resettled
and EGAT has included for this purpose a sum of $ 120 million or 3.7% of
total construction expenditure. This is equivalent to US$750 per inhabitant
and is considered to be adequate; it would be about 50% higher than the amount
contemplated for the proposed Pa Mong project on the Mekong River and about
three times the amount for the Volta river project in Ghana. It will be
essential to prepare a detailed resettlement plan, primarily to ensure that
the resettled population can earn a living under conditions at least equal
to those now existing. The preparation of this plan will be the responsibi-
lity of a coordinating committee consisting of, but not limited to: EGAT;
the Departments of Public Welfare and Public Health, Credit and Marketing
Cooperatives, Fisheries and Forestry, Land Cooperation and Development;
the Royal Irrigation Department; and the Ministry of Education. In addition
the plan will take into account the views of the population to be resettled.
During negotiations assurances were obtained that: (i) the Committee would
be established by May 31, 1974; (ii) the detailed plan will be submitted to
the Bank for approval by December 31, 1974; (iii) EGAT would be made responsi-
ble for the physical execution of the plan; and (iv) the Government would
provide any funds needed in excess of $ 120 million should this amount
prove to be inadequate for the purpose.
V. PROJECT JUSTIFICATION
The Power Market
5.01      At the end of 1962, EGAT's predecessors served a maximum
demand of 113 MW and generated 512 GWh. The average annual load factor



- 15 -
was 51.6%. ?en years later, in 1972, maximum demand had increased to
1,030 MW, generation to 5,711 GWh and the annual load factor had improved
to 63.3%. In the ten year period, there was a ten-fold increase in power
and energy requirements. Average annual growth rates were 25% for demand
and 27% for energy. These growth rates, which varied from year to year,
correlated closely with economic developments. Early stimulants were
rapidly rising investments, favorable world rice markets, and export
of services (US military). The turning point came in 1969 due to a combina-
tion of a decline in US military expenditures and transfers, and a reduction
in the prices of rubber and rice. The low point was reached in 1971
when demand and energy requirements increased by only 15.0% and 17.2% respec-
tively. However, system growth recovered in 1972 to better than 19.0%.
5.02      For Thailand as a whole per capita generation of electricity
increased from 85 kwh in 1968 to 153 kwh in 1972 at an average annual rate
of 15.2%. The number of electricity consumers increased in this period
from 694,514 to 967,462 and generation/consumer from 3,980 kwh to 6,015 kwh.
In spite of these impressive statistics, only 17% of the total Thai
population (3.6 million within Bangkok and 2.8 million outside Bangkok)
enjoy the benefit of electricity. Thus the latent demand to be served
remains substantial.
5.03      Of total power sold throughout the country in 1972, residential
sales accounted for 20.4%; industrial and commercial sales for 78.8% and
street lighting for 0.8%. In Bangkok, the capital, residential sales
amounted in 1972 to 2,020 kwh/consumer, whilst in the rest of the country
the corresponding figure was 735 kwh. The growth rate of residential con-
sumption per consumer in the Bangkok metropolitan area averaged 8.0% during
1968-1972 whilst in the provinces a rate of 12.1% was achieved. This
illustrates to an extent improving economic development of the provincial
regions.
5.04      The power market forecast is based on known industrial developments
and the Government's 1972-1976 Economic Development Plan. Maximum demand
to be served by EGAT in 1982 is forecast at about 3,260 MW and generation
at 19,250 GWh. This indicates average annual growth rates for 1972-1982
of 12.1% for demand and 13.0% for generation, substantially below historic
rates because of the larger base and expected slower economy growth. On a
national basis generation/capita would increase from 153 kwh in 1972 to
382 kwh in 1982 (average growth rate 9.8% compared to 15.8% for the period
1968-1972). By 1982 an estimated 27% of the population would enjoy the
benefits of electricity. In 1982 EGAT is forecast to provide for 96% of all
power demand in Thailand (the corresponding 1968 figure was 88.6%). Power
demand is not distorted by an inadequate tariff policy (see also para 3.10).
Further details on passt and forecast development of the power market are
given in the tables of Annex 20.
Economic Evaluation
5.05      Because the project will provide measurable agricultural benefits
downstream, the Government agreed in 1970 to provide $ 600 million (about



- 16 -
US$30 million equivalent) as equity towards the cost of the dam. The
methodology used in arriving at this allocation was the acceptable" Separable
Costs Remaining Benefits Method".
5.06      Three alternatives were considered in order to analyse the merits
of the proposed project:
(a) comparison of the proposed project with an oil-fired steam
alternative providing the fame service, 1/ assuming the
proposed project to bear
(i) all costs; and
(ii) all costs less the $ 600 million allocated to irrigation.
The comparison was based on the discounted cash flows of the
two alternatives over a period of 50 years. To allow for
uncertainties, a probability analysis was used to establish
the mean value and range of variation of the discount rate
which equalized the present worth of the two alternatives,
assuming three different values, with corresponding probabilities
assigned to them, for each of the main variables (capital costs
and fuel price);
(b) determination of the equalizing discount rate of a cost and
benefit stream over 50 years, of a downstream irrigation
project. This analysis was carried out on a sensitivity
basis with: the most probable costs and benefits; costs
increased by 20% and probable benefits; benefits decreased
by 25% and probable costs; and costs increased by 20% and
benefits decreased by 25%. In carrying out this analysis
it was assumed that
(i) no Quae Yai costs would be allocated to irrigation;
and
(ii) S 600 million of Quae Yai costs would be allocated to
irrigation; and
(c) comparison of an alternative power development stream
containing oil-fired steam generation, but no irrigation, 2/
with a power development stream containing the proposed
1/ System effects could be ignored in this case because of the modern
and efficient plant already in service.
2/   An irrigation project alone, bearing the full costs of storage facili-
ties to provide the necessary regulation, would not be economically
viable.



- 17 -
project and an irrigation project. Total costs includirg
operating and maintenance costs of the multipurpose project
were reduced by the incremental benefits 1/ attributable to
irrigation thus giving a net multipurpose cost stream.
Power benefits were ignored since they are common to both
alternatives. This analysis was carried out over 50 years
on a sensitivity basis with: the most probable capital
and fuel costs and probable irrigation benefits; the upper
range of hydro costs, 20% higher irrigation costs, 25% lower
irrigation benefits; higher range of thermal costs (capital
and fuel), low hydro costs, most probable irrigation costs,
and irrigation benefits increased by 25%.
5.07      The range of equalizing discount rates computed for the above
alternatives permit realistic assessment of the influence of value varia-
tions on the main parameters. The rates are:

particular project.

- 18 -
5.08      The above results justify implementation of the proposed power
project, especially since the analysis attributed no value to benefits that
can be realized subsequent to the scheme's implementation such as tourism
(close proximity to Bangkok), fisheries in the reservoir, flood control (5
and 5C year return floods would become 15 and 1000 year return floods), and
communication in the valley above the dam. However, the substantial down-
stream agriculture/irrigation benefits that can be realized improves the
overall situation, indicating that early implementation of an agriculture/
irrigation project should be aimed at. Further details of the July 1973
analysis are given in Annexes 1 and 20.
Financial Justification of the Project
5.09      The financial rate of return of the Project, defined as the discount
rate which equalizes the Project's cost stream (with the Project bearing all
costs) and its associated benefit stream (tariffs prevailing before the
adjustment for increased fuel costs) is about 11.2%. This is a satisfactory
level, coincides with the opportunity cost of capital, and indicates that
base tariff levels are appropriate. With the 55% tariff increase to offset
increased fuel costs the financial rate of return of the project would
increase to about 15.3%.
VI. FINANCIAL ASPECTS
Past Operating Results and Present Financial Position
6.01      The provisions of the Act governing EGAT's activities and the
policies followed enabled the Authority's management to maintain a sound
financial position. For the past four fiscal years, the rate of return on
average net fixed assets in operation varied between 7.9% (1970) and 10.1%
(1971); debt service coverage on an annual basis was better than 1.6 times;
self-financing averaged about 30% of capital investments; the debt/equity
ratio of 58/42 (1973) indicated a satisfactory capital structure; and a
current ratio of about 1.7 (1973) was adequate. Income Statements and
Balance Sheets for 1970-1973 and 1969-1973 respectively are shown in
Annexes 21 and 22.
Financial Forecasts
6.02      EGAT's future financial prospects as compared to those of a
year ago are significantly affected by recent fuel price increases and
currency adjustments, since the Baht (with the exception of a 4% upward
adjustment vis-a-vis the US$ in July 1973) followed the US$. Outstanding
debt service obligations in currencies other than the US$ have increased,
and new investments expressed in Baht and thus future foreign debt are
higher. The amounts in absolute terms are considerable. These are esti-
mated for the period 1974-1982 as follows:
(a) existing debt service -- up $ 200 million; and
(b) capital investments -- up $ 550 million.



- 19 -
6.03      Several sets of financial projections were prepared during
appraisal to consider the variables available in analyzing measures required
to maintain the past sound financial position in light of the changed
situation mentioned in the previous paragraph. The principal variables
considered were:
(a) reduce operating expenses (since fuel costs and depreciation
account for roughly 75% of this account, there is no signifi-
canlt room for improvement);
(b) reduce capital construction (this was done in terms of
system capability by cutting reserves to the lowest
acceptable level, with some risk. Nevertheless, the
reduced program is still more expensive in terms of
Baht than was the previous larger program);
(c) introduce a fuel adjustment clause in the tariff structure;
(d) increase tariffs; and
(e) extend a previously-agreed tax moratorium beyond 1976.
In addition, there was scope to vary the amounts and type of debt to be
incurred and to examine cost-sharing assumptions for multipurpose project
construction undertaken by EGAT.
Financing Plan
6.04      The proposed financing plan resulting from the above analysis is
summarized below.  It excludes the effect of the fuel surcharge as does the
subsequent discussion of the financial forecasts.

6.05      The proposed project would be financed by a Bank loan of US$75.0
million equivalent (41.5%); an OECF loan of US$41.0 million equivalent
(22.5%); a local currency loan of US$4.5 million equivalent (2.5%) to cover
import duties; equity contributions of US$29.5 million equivalent (16.5%);
and retained earnings of US$31.0 million equivalent (17.0%), a total of
about US$181.0 million equivalent. The proposed project would represent
13% of EGAT's 1974-1982 capital program (Annex 11). A Sources and Applica-
tions of Funds Statement is given in Annex 23.
6.06      Government has agreed, and the proposed Loan and Guarantee Agree-
ments provide for the translation into action of the assumptions underlying
the above financing plan, namely that:
(a) a tariff increase to compensate for the difference
between the fuel price prevailing on the date of
the increase and the price on July 1, 1973
(US$0.50 per million Btu) will be made effective
not later than June 1, 1974;
(b) a fuel adjustment will be introduced into the
tariff structure to increase or decrease the basic
energy charges to compensate for subsequent changes
in the cost of fuel;
(c) the Government will provide equity of $ 600 million
towards the cost of the project as a reasonable
contribution for downstream benefits;
(d) the Government will provide EGAT with a loan of
$ 90 million to cover estimated import duty costs
of the project; and
(e) the Government will assist EGAT in issuing bonds
equivalent to $ 300 million.
6.07      The Council of Ministers has agreed to extend the existing income
tax moratorium to 1982 and also that EGAT shall maintain its income at a
level sufficient to contribute 30% of the cost of investment in power
facilities. This will require a tariff increase of about 5% in addition
to the increase to offset the increase in oil prices.
6.08      The receipt by EGAT of a letter of intent from OECF confirming
their intention to make available to EGAT an amount equivalent to V 11.6
billion would be a condition of effectiveness of the loan. The terms of
the OECF loan were assumed at 3.25% with a 25-year term including 7 years
grace on amortization.
Future Operating Results (The following discussion excludes the effect on
revenue or cost of variations in fuel price as the fuel surcharge is
designed to "wash" these out.)



- 22 -
General
6.09      Energy sales are estimated to increase from 6,399 GWh in 1973 to
17,500 GWh in 1982 at an average annual growth rate of about 12Z. The
average revenue per kwh sold is estimated to average about $ 0.30 (USe 1.5).
While revenues are forecast to increase from $ 1,832 million in 1973 to
$ 5,734 million in 1982 at an average annual growth rate of about 12%,
operating expenses are forecast to increase at an average growth rate of
about 13%, an indicator that a further tariff increase may be necessary
towards the end of the decade.
Rate of Return
6.10      The rate of return on average net fixed assets in operation 1974-
1982 is estimated to be not lower than 8.2% (1974) and would exceed 10% in
1976-1980.  The decline towards the end of the forecast period when the
first nuclear plant enters the rate base is a further indication of a
possible need for upward tariff adjustments in these years.
Debt/Equity
6.11      EGAT's capital structure remains favorable.  The debt/equity ratio
remains around 58/42 throughout the forecast period.
Operatin  Ratio
6.12      While this ratio remains satisfactory at around 60% over most
of the forecast period, its upward trend in 1981-82 gives further indica-
tion that a tariff adjustment may be needed toward the end of the period
under review.
Current Ratio
6.13      This ratio hag varied between 1.26 and 1.67 in the past and will
not drop below 1.34, a satisfactory level. Since EGAT sells power in bulk
to a limited number of consumers, its accounts receivable position has been
forecast to improve from 2-1/2 months' revenues in 1973 to 1-1/2 months'
revenues by 1977. The inventory level is adequate. Year-end cash require-
ments are forecast to increase from $ 110 million in 1973 to % 290 million
in 1982, a target not met in all years. However, with its overdraft
facilities of $ 200 million, EGAT should have no difficulties in meeting
its day-to-day commitments. It is financially advantageous for EGAT to
meet unexpected short-term cash requirements through utilization of its
overdraft facilities.
Debt Control
6.14      On an annual basis debt-service coverage averages about 1.8 times,
which is satisfactory. However, the current debt control covenant prescribes
that, except as the Bank and the Borrower shall otherwise agree, internal



- 23 -
cash generation of the past fiscal year or a later 12-month period prior
to the incurrence of debt shall be not less than 1.4 times future maximum
debt service on all debt drawn. The coverage on this basis would vary
between 1.22 and 1.44 during the forecast period. The intent of this
covenant was to provide a test which, if applied and not met, would cause
the Borrower to consult the Bank before incurring debt.  Since debt is
defined as incurred only at the time of drawdown, strict application of
the covenant would require the Bank's agreement to every debt drawing to
be made during the next four or five years.
6.15      The form of the earnings test (paras. 3.09 and 6.16) ensures
adequate debt service coverage regardless of the volume of debt. What is
needed in the circumstances is control over the incurrence of debt, not
its drawdown. For this, a simple type of debt control covenant was agreed
during negotiations. It would give EGAT's management adequate freedom to
manage its debt while providing for Bank review of project financing in-
volving substantial amounts. The proposed Loan Agreement provides:
(a) "The Borrower covenants that before it shall:
Mi) undertake or execute, for its own account
or for the account of any third party or
parties, any new major investment 1/ not
related to the Project; or
(ii) acquire any major asset, 1/ it shall first
have obtained the agreement of the Bank to
the financing plan covering such project,
investment or asset"; and
(b)  "Except as the Bank and the Borrower shall from
time to time agree, the Borrower shall not incur
short term debt, including overdraft arrangements
and bonds, if by such incurrence the Borrower's
total outstanding short term indebtedness would
exceed a sum e'quivalent to US$50,000,000."
Self-Financing
6.16      Under the existing loan agreements with the Bank, EGAT is required
to establish and maintain tariffs which will provide sufficient revenues to
cover operating expenses including depreciation, interest, debt amortiza-
tion insofar as it exceeds depreciation, and to finance, on average, not
less than 30% of the investments in power facilities during any consecu-
tive four years comprising one actual and three forecast years. This
1/   Defined as involving an investment of more than US$50 million
equivalent.



- 24 -
eirnings test, which differs in form although not in substance from the
more usual return on assets test, has served its purpose very well in the
past. It reflects the requirements of the EGAT Act, which the Bank
approved, and follows the Government's policy requiring publicly-owned
companies to rely on a reasonable degree of self-financing.
6.17      As shown in the table of paragraph 6.04, EGAT will contribute
30% towards construction from internally generated funds over the period
1974-1982 assuming a tariff increase of about 5% from the beginning of
FY 1975.  The financial projections as given in the Sources and Applications
of Funds Statements, shown in Annex 23, include, however, the issuance
of local bonds of % 300 million in 1974. Together with a previous
issue of $ 50 million in 1972 and l 234 million in 1973, these bonds,
all with a maturity of 5 years, are scheduled for retirement in 1977,
1978, and 1979. EGAT's cash position in these years would permit
their retirement and the forecast assumes that EGAT would do so. Since
the bonds are issued and retired in the period under consideration, their
exclusion (interest component excepted) from the calculation of the
contribution to construction percentage is reasonable, giving the above-
mentioned figure of 30%. In application of the covenant covering successive
4-year periods, the exclusion of the bonds is also reasonable in view of
their short-term nature. Thus the covenanted requirement of 30% is met
in all years except 1974 (28%). The reason for the shortfall in that year
is attributable to the currency exchange rate adjustments of December 1971
and February 1973 and because the assumed tariff increase does not become
effective until the beginning of 1975. For instance, the shortfall in
foreign exchange of the two current Bank loans (655-TH and 790-TH) is
estimated at US$14.5 million (S 290 million). Debt service payments and
costs of other projects are also affected. To offset this shortfall,
EGAT will issue short-term local bonds for public and commercial bank
subscription in these years.
6.18      In spite of these difficulties EGAT's forecast position is
satisfactory and can be summarized as follows:
(a) EGAT will earn a rate of return on net fixed assets
in operation averaging about 9.8% for the period, a
satisfactory level;
(b) the debt/equity ratio does not fall below 59/41,
indicating a satisfactory capital structure; and
(c) the debt/service coverage on an annual basis
averages 1.8, which is adequate.
6.19      Inclusion of interest during construction in the proposed Bank
loan is recommended because:
(a) EGAT's past and projected financial position is
sound;



- 25 -
(b) it represents foreign exchange expenditure; and
(c) EGAT's financial situation requires it or its
equivalent in other borrowings.
Debtors
6.20      EGAT had no consumers in serious arrears at September 30, 1973.
VII.  AGREEMENTS REACHED AND RECOMNENDATION
7.01      During loan negotiations agreement was reached on the following
points and appropriate covenants included in the agreement for the
proposed loan:
(a) an earnings test (paras. 3.09 and 6.16);
(b) resettlement (para. 4.13);
(c)  tariff increase (para. 6.06); and
(d) debt control (para. 6.15).
7.02      The receipt of a letter of intent from OECF by EGAT confirming
OECF's intention to help finance the project is a condition of effective-
ness of the proposed loan (paras. 4.03 and 6.08).
7.03      The proposed project constitutes a suitable basis for a Bank
loan of US$75.0 million to the Electricity Generating Authority of
Thailand for a period of 26 years including a grace period of 6 years.






ANNEX 1.1
Page 1
THAILAND
ELECTRICITY GENERATING AUTHORITY OF THAILAND
QUAE YAI HYDRO-ELECTRIC PROJECT
IRRIGATION ASPECTS
introduction
1.        Tlhe Mae Klong (or Meklong) River Plain forms the southwestern
portion of the Central Plain of Thailand. The main population center,
Nakhon Pathom, is situated 138 km west of Bangkok. The climate is tropical:
the winter or northeast monsoon season extends from October to Februarv;
the summer or hot season from February to May; and the wet or southwest
monsoon season from May to October. The mean annual rainfall is approxi-
mately 1,100 mm, of which 85% falls during the wet season. Without irriga-
tion, crop production in the dry season is extremely limited while wet
season yields are uncertain due to the likelihood of short dry periods at
the beginning of the wet season.
2.        The potential for irrigation development from the Mae Klong River
is about 400,000 ha. The bulk of this area is on the left bank and slopes
gently towards the Nakhon Chaisri River. Due to the many old rivers, terraces,
and channels, the terrain is somewhat undulating. Large areas are inundated
each wet season and, without better water control, are suitable only for
floating rice. Soil surveys have shown that about two-thirds of the Plain
is best suited for rice production, tohacco, peanuts and vegetables.
3.        According to a 1966 census, about 860,000 persons or 144,000
families are dependent upon agriculture in the Plain. Approximately 70%
of the holdings, comprising 65% of the land, are between 2 and 4 ha; while
only 8% are less than 2 ha. Some rather large holdings exist in the areas
where broadcast rice-growing is practiced. About 70% of the holdings were
owner-operated in 1967, but the expansion of sugar growing on rented land
may have changed this proportion.
The Mae Klong Stage I Project (Loan 394-TH)
4.        In 1964, the Bank made a loan of US$22 million to Thailand for a
first stage project in the Mae Klong Plain (Loan 394-TH). The purpose of
the project was to provide regulated (wet-season) irrigation, surface drain-
age, and partial flood control to 175,000 ha on the left bank (known as



ANNEX 1.1
Page 2
the Stage I area); to carry out land classification of the entire Mae Klong
Plain (390,000 ha); and to conduct a feasibility study for a second stage
project.  Major features of the project, as envisaged at appraisal, included:
(a) the Vajiralongkorn diversion barrage across the Mae Klong
River at Tha Muang;
(b) a main canal about 70 km in length and about 540 km of
secondary and tertiary canals;
(c)  flood protection dikes totalling 102 km;
(d) 68 km of new major drains and improvements to about 203 km
of minor channels;
(e) 40 km of feeder roads;
(f) a detailed land classification survey over the entire Plain;
(g) the establishment and operation of an experimental and
demonstration farm in the light-textured soils of the
northwest portion of the Plain;
(h) a feasibility study for a second stage project; and
(i) the services of advisers and individual consultants for
carrying out the various aspects of the project.
5.        The physical works were constructed by the Royal Irrigation Depart-
ment (RID) by force account. Construction began in 1965 and is now
essentially complete, except for some of the minor drainage ditches and
the flood protection dike which was deleted from the project (see para 7).
Construction took about two years longer than expected, but the estimate of
total costs was not exceeded. In fact, there were considerable savings
in the foreign exchange requirements and approximately US$5,364,000 of
the loan amount was cancelled after the closing date of June 30, 1970
(extended from December 31, 1969).
6.        Concrete Lining - Early in the construction period, RID adopted
the policy of concrete-lining all canals. The economic justification of
lining canals in the relatively impermeable soils of the project area was
never adequately established and the Bank, therefore, decided to exclude
expenditures for lining from financing out of the loan. However, canal
lining was executed outside the scope of the Bank-financed project at a
cost of about US$10 million. While this work will certainly facilitate
water control, especially in the dry season and should increase irrigation
efficiency, it is doubtful whether the benefits have exceeded the costs.
RID has since abandoned the policy of lining all canals and, on future
projects in this area, lining will be limited to sections where it is
justified by high seepage losses.



ANNEX 1.1
Page 3
Flood Protection - During the construction period, it was found
that the land acquisition cost for the proposed 97 km left bank flood
protection dike would be much higher than expected at appraisal, due to
accelerated industrial and residential development adjacent to the river.
As RID was at that stage planning to construct storage reservoirs on the
Quae Yai and Quae Noi Rivers, the major tributaries of the Mae Klong, it
appeared that the proposed dike would not be required in the long term.
Therefore, the dike was eliminated from the project and a 1 km overflow
section was incorporated into the main canal, which runs close to the left
bank of the river, so that flood waters could escape to the southeast
without damage to the irrigation facilities. The Quae Yai reservoir now
proposed will certainly reduce the likelihood of flooding but, as the Quae
Noi reservoir is unlikely to be built for some years, if at all, it would
be necessary to examine the question of flood protection for the Mae Klong
Plain. Studies to date have not attempted to quantify the benefits of
alternative methods of flood mitigation, except indirectly through the
projection of higher crop yields.
8.        Irrigation Effectiveness - The purpose of the Mae Klong Project
was to improve water control for wet season irrigation. Therefore, there
was no provision in the project for on-farm works, such as farm ditches and
drains and land levelling. Consequently, little development of this kind
has taken place and yields have remained rather low. The area irrigable
from the Mae Klong Project works is 149,000 ha. The reduction in area from
the 175,000 ha estimated at appraisal reflects the preliminary status of
design at appraisal, the infeasibility of cormanding some of the more
elevated land, and inadequate methods of canal design, which resulted in
some canals being constructed too low to irrigate their full command areas.
The wet season area actually irrigated was 22,500 ha in 1971 and 108,000 ha
in 1972. It is expected that the full 149,000 ha will be irrigated in 1973.
At appraisal, it was expected that a small area of 8,000 ha would be irri-
gated in the dry season under Stage I but to date, no significant amount
of dry-season irrigation has taken place.
9.        Agricultural Development - Rice is the major crop and occupies
60 to 70% of the cultivated area. A range of native rice varieties is
grown, which vary in duration, straw length and ability to withstand
variation in water depth and flood duration. About 45% of the rice area
is low-lying and subject to flooding, and thus is suitable only for broad-
cast cultivation with minimal use of modern inputs. The remaining rice
land has some degree of water control and transplanting is practiced, along
with some use of fertilizer and agrochemicals. Sugarcane is also an impor-
tant crop and the Mae Klong Plain accounts for half of Thailand's production.
However, yields are comparatively low.
10.       Paddy yields at the time of appraisal in 1964 ranged from 1.0
to 1.5 ton/ha in various parts of the project area. It was estimated that
yields would rise to 1.7 to 2.8 ton/ha after full development of the first



ANNEX 1.1
Page 4
stage project. Thus, the present yields of 1.3 ton/ha for native broadcast
rice, 1.9 ton/ha for native transplanted rice and 2.8 ton/ha for RDI trans-
planted rice ( a high-yielding variety) appear to be reasonably in line
with expectations, remembering that the full development period assumed for
the first stage project has not yet elapsed.
11.       These results have been achieved despite inadequate levels of
agricultural supporting services such as seed, fertilizer, credit and
extension services. The extension service, provided by the Ministry of
Agriculture is severely limited in its effectiveness by the lack of adequate
funds, facilities and trained personnel. The ratio of extension workers
to farmers is of the order of 1:5,000. The lack of supporting services
could be an impediment to the full realization of benefits from the Stage I
project and any future projects in the Mae Klong Plain should specifically
address these needs. The experimental and demonstration farm included in
the Stage I project has only recentlv been established and has not yet had
any impact on the area.
12.       Future Development - The irrigation facilities constructed under
Loan 394-TH are unable to provide significant amounts of water in the dry
season, as the Vajiralongkorn Barrage has virtually no storage capacity,
and the unregulated flows of the Mae Klong River are highly seasonal. The
construction of the Quae Yai Dam would make available a reliable dry-season
water stupply for about 235,000 ha. However, to make effective use of tnis
water, especially where soils are best suited to non-rice crops, on-farm
development would be necessary. As the organizational capacity of the
Ministry of Agriculture to carry out such works is limited to about 20,000
ha per year, it is necessary to carefully re-assess priorities for develop-
ment between various parts of the Mae Klong Plain, in order to maximize
the economic returns to investment.
13.       When the Stage I project was appraised in 1964, it was envisaged
that the next stage of development would be the provision of irrigation
facilities to the same level as provided for Stage I (that is, without on-
farm development) to an area of 220,000 ha (140,000 to the north of the
Stage I area and 80,000 ha on the right bank of the Mae Klong, as shown
on the attached Map. A feasibility study under Loan 394-TH was conducted
by RID with the assistance of advisers from the United States Bureau of
Reclamation and was completed in 1968. In accordance with this plan, RID
has constructed, over the last two years, about 50 km of the main canal,
together with a number of laterals to serve this Stage II area.
14.       Taking into account experience from pilot projects in the Chao
Phya Plain north of Bangkok, an analysis was made of the benefits to be
obtained from development of the Stage II area for wet-season cultivation
only. This shows that a rate of return of only 6% may be expected. Addi-
tional investment, mainly in on-farm development, is needed to permit dry-
season cropping and to give the degree of water control necessary to maximize



ANNEX 1.1
Page 5
yields from high-yielding rice varieties and non-rice crops. If these
additional investments are included and dry-season cropping is assumed, the
economic rate of return is acceptable.
15.       It is, therefore, proposed that over the next few years, invest-
ment should be channelled ftrst to providing on-farm development to the
.Stage I area and later to providing full irrigation facilities, including
on-farm works, to the Stage II area. As the rate of development would be
governed by the availability of funds and experienced staff, it would not
be possible to proceed with on-farm development works on both areas simul-
taneously. Therefore, in order to carry out the proposed program, it would
be necessary for RID to postpone further construction in the Stage II area.
Recommendations are given below for the steps needed to implement the
phased introduction of dry-season cropping in the Mae Klong Plain.
The Mae Klong Irrigation Improvement Project
16.       The proposed Mae Klong Improvement Project would provide on-farm
development and the necessary supporting services at adequate levels to
permit year-round cultivation in the Stage I area previously assisted under
Loan 394-TH.  In view of the considerable past investments in irrigation
infrastructure in this area, and the fact that the Quae Yai Dam would pro-
vide a regulated water supply in the dry-season, the economic rate of return
is likely to be reasonably high. On-farm development comprises; land
levelling, realignment of farm boundaries, to enable a more efficient
irrigation and drainage layout; farm ditches and drains; and farm roads.
Up to about 110,000 ha of the project area would be physically suitable for
development at this intensity. Further drainage works, feed roads and
possibly some additional structures in ,;he main canals would also be
required. Supporting services would include expansion of the extension
service, training of extension workers, and provision of seeds, fertilizer
and other ipputs at reasonable prices and with adequate sources of credit.
Preliminary estimates suggest that such a project, which would cover 150,000
ha for vet season cropping and 84,000 ha in the dry season, would cost about
t 900 million (US$43 million). Additional details on irrigated areas and
cropping patterns are given in pages 8 and 9, and a detailed cost estimate
is given on page 10 of this Annex.
17.       Some study has also been given to a future extension of the pro-
ject into the Stage II area of 220,000 ha, which has been divided into four
sul-areas for analysis. The cost of full development, including the main
irrigation system and on-farm works, would be US$136 million at present
prices. It is likely that this project would have to be broken into several
stages. Due to commitments elsewhere in the country, it is doubtful whether
the Government could implement this kind of development at a rate greater
than 20,000 ha per year.

Page 6
